  13. **Update 4 July 2011** Will eventually rewrite this review using long-term results. Using too few pulses will lead to no reduction in hair growth, or at best thinner hairs, because insufficient heat was absorbed to destroy all hair-producing cells, even if it was enough to weaken the hair root allowing the hair to fall out. Growth might be slow, but eventually the hair will grow back. To prevent this from happening, it is essential to use enough pulses to completely remove the hair follicle on the first try, since later passes in the months following will both consume a large amount of time, and will have lower chances of success if the hair has become thinner. This means knowing how many pulses are enough to simply make the hair fall out, and then exceeding that number to ensure the follicle is completely destroyed. To gather this data, the original suggestion of epilating prior to using TRIA should not be followed, since the best way to check if TRIA is working is to use tweezers, or even your fingers to check if the hair can be easily removed several seconds after finishing the series of pulses. By far the most significant factors in applying enough heat to the follicle are wetting the skin, which both provides cooling from evaporation and also moderates the temperature increase of the outer skin surface preventing burns; cooling with ice, beforehand and possibly between TRIA pulses; and applying all pulses to a specific hair follicle in rapid succession, instead of moving away from the area and later returning multiple times to overlap coverage. Heat dissipates very quickly from a hair to the surrounding area, but the follicle only needs to be at a high enough temperature for a few moments. Also, work in patches since this method is very slow and the lack of progress can be discouraging without a visible contrast between completed areas. Guidelines: &nbsp; - The relatively thick hairs found in particular areas can be removed with no resistance with aslittle as 1~2 full-power pulses, but to prevent regrowth this number needs to be increased. I am currently testing having used 3~4 pulses in rapid succession, with both ice (which cools the follicle as well) and wetting the skin (which mainly prevents burns). &nbsp; - For legs, applying pulses in overlapping lines (moving about half the diameter of treatment window after each pulse, so each follicle receiving 2~3 pulses during a pass) lead to significant reduction of growth for several months, but many (40~70%) regrew at a similar or thinner width. A thinner hair just means more pulses are needed to remove it again, if it can be removed at all. Currently testing 4~6 pulses in rapid succession with ice beforehand and wetting the skin, which seems to be enough to remove most hairs in the correct growth phase (thinner hairs that aren't growing and don't hurt when lasered are just pulled out after several pulses to avoid confusion and wasting pulses). &nbsp; - For arms, while hairs are smaller than on legs they are comparable in size to the thinner hairs that result from insufficient pulses on legs. While I have tried to do arms several times, ranging from several pulses on power 4 (out of 5) with cooling to a full-power pulse with no cooling to 2 pulses per hair without cooling, this significantly underestimated the number of pulses necessary for hairs of this size. Now have several test patches, which required as many as 6~8 pulses (with cooling prior and once during) for the targeted hairs to be easily removed with no resistance. &nbsp; - Armpits/underarms: Several attempts for the entire areas. The hairs might have reduced in size, not sure since nothing to compare them to, but the technique used simply did not apply enough heat, and overlapping coverage just caused pain because there was too much time to dissipate heat between passes. The method of testing ease of removal seems to be the most reliable way to know how many pulses are needed, but currently for meother areas have priority. It is easy to vastly underestimate how much time may be needed to permanently remove hairs using the TRIA! Using just 1~2 pulses at full power may take a moderate amount of time comparable to say epilating, but this will be completely ineffective at permanently removing hairs, much less when judging based off the smaller amount of time to cover an area at a lower power setting. Test the effectiveness by pulling out a representative hair after using TRIA on it, or risk having to do the same area again (having fewer hairs in the 1cm window does not mean it goes faster!) using even more pulses per hair a few months later when the hairs in that area regrow! Hairs using a smaller number of pulses have taken significantly longer to regrow than from epilation (2 months as opposed to 3 weeks) and are thinner than before, but the area still has to be redone. If this regrowth can be prevented by increasing the number of pulses, this review will be updated and condensed to reflect that result. **end update** Original review: First and foremost: some pain is necessary, but most pain is unnecessary! Whether or not the TRIA laser is effective depends on several factors&#8212; &nbsp;&#8227; The colour of the skin and hair, but also... &nbsp;&#8227; Depth of the hair follicle from the skin surface. &nbsp;&#8227; Size of the follicle. &nbsp;&#8227; Width of the hair at the surface. &nbsp;&#8227; Number of hairs within the area of the treatment head (hair density). If enough laser light is delivered to the hair follicle within a small enough amount of time, it will heat up to the point that the hair follicle is destroyed. The two main reasons that this temperature is not reached are the sections of hairs at the surface of the skin heating to the point of causing localized damage, or a general rise in temperature of the entire area of skin being treated to the point that damage results. The second effect can be mitigated by cooling the skin and continuing to direct laser pulses towards the follicle; but the first, of damage at the surface around hairs, can only be addressed by removing the hairs to prevent them from absorbing laser light at the skin's surface. According to the instructions epilation should be avoided for 4~6 weeks prior to the first use of TRIA laser. This may be fine for those with the most ideal skin tones, since most of the laser light can reach the follicle and hairs that are slightly visible after shaving help guide where to use the laser. Those who do not have ideal skin tones should consider the following on whether to epilate prior to TRIA laser use: &nbsp;&#8227; Is the area of skin being treated darker than other areas of your body? &nbsp;&#8227; Do the hairs come straight out, or are they slanted making the roots closer to the skin surface? &nbsp;&#8227; How thick are the hairs at this location? &nbsp;&#8227; How dense is the hair growth? All of these combined, on if you should epilate can be answered with one simple result from using the TRIA laser: It hurts!! And what's more, even if you withstand a full treatment of the area, it will have virtually no effect since not enough light is reaching the follicles despite a similar intensity working perfectly fine to remove hair on other areas of your body. This is what tells you of the need to epilate that area for TRIA to work. My own experience: Tried TRIA on lowest setting and it hurt so much I waited for a satin smooth res-q pain relief product to arrive. After an hour with a very generous coat of 4% lidocaine product applied, the area felt somewhat numb and the pain was almost bearable for a moderate power setting with the TRIA laser. However, despite the overall temperature of the area of skin feeling very warm and pain relief cream to the point that a tiny amount seeped inside the treatment head to the other side of the transparent window forming a small, clear yellow spot, the pain was still intense and despite using the entire battery charge with a power setting of 3~4 and repeating areas as dictated by the instructions, there was no noticeable reduction in hair growth except at the very edges of the area where hairs grew slanted with the roots close to the skin's surface. What did happen, was it seemed oil glands opening on to the hair shafts had been damaged by the intense heat flux, causing a crusty residue around the hairs and other signs of damage to the skin immediately surrounding each hair! And yet a week later, those same hairs had seen no reduction in growth rate. Next: using cold water to cool the skin, without the pain relief product, to try to focus the effect of TRIA laser on the roots of the follicles. Another full battery charge later, surprisingly with the same amount or less pain due to the numbing action of cold on surrounding nerves, there was again no noticeable reduction of hair in that area. Finally resolving to try epilation again, which has problems in similar situations of relatively thick hairs and dense growth except with the added complication of skin tautness being needed to prevent additional (unnecessary) pain. It may even be necessary to use tweezers, which may take several hours but as you'll see it's worth it... The next attempt was two days after epilation. It still huuurt, even with absolutely no visible hair growth, even while using ice to numb the entire area! Then again another two days after that. The result as seen several weeks later... &nbsp;&#8227; 95% reduction of hairs rate on areas of 2~3 pulses on maximum power average coverage. &nbsp;&#8227; 60% reduction of hairs (uneven) on areas of 1.5~2 pulses on maximum power, due to bending to reduce the amount of pulses needed to cover the area, instead of trying to stretch the skin to bring roots of the follicles closer to the surface of the skin. On a different area with similar hair density, overlapping coverage of 2~3 pulses on cooled skin, one day after epilation, has lead to approximately 90% reduction of hairs at that area four weeks after a single session of TRIA laser, despite that the skin was actually slightly too dark to register as green on the skin sensor compared to skin tone of the surrounding areas. An agonizing session a week beforehand had lead to practically zero reduction of growth and even a slight burn due to over-application of laser light >.< Even when using ice to cool! A nearby region with slightly less dark skin (registering green on sensor) with slanting hairs and follicles close to the surface and equivalent density seemed to not have resulted in significant reduction prior to epilation, but a month afterwards that particular area is down 60~80% from normal (patchy) despite not having gone over that area a second time, but this unexpected result was due to the direction of hair growth allowing much more of the light to reach the hair roots instead of just being absorbed at the surface. So as you can see, if you are accustomed to epilating before making the choice to invest in the TRIA laser, don't hesitate to do so one last time several days before using the TRIA on an area with relatively small follicles such as the leg, or the day before or even the day of for areas with somewhat larger hairs like the delicate zone. You will probably not have a reason to do so later on as identifying single hairs will become the focus instead of broad swaths of laser pulse application. Other things to keep in mind: &nbsp;&#8227; While using ice to cool the entire area does reduce pain, it also increases the number of pulses that must be applied per unit area. &nbsp;&#8227; A momentary touch from ice or another cold object can cool the skin surface enough to keep it from being damaged for those with darker skin tones, while not propagating deeper within the skin before the destruction of the hair follicles can occur from repeated laser pulses. &nbsp;&#8227; Just like with electrolysis, when the follicle is destroyed the resistance of the hair to being pulled out weakens drastically. If a hair doesn't do this when you apply the usual number of pulses, try tweezing it out and you'll probably see the hair narrowing as it approached the follicle and a pale dot at its end, which didn't absorb sufficient laser light to die and means the hair was in the wrong growth phase. &nbsp;&#8227; Aim for the root of the follicle! When cleaning up isolated hairs on your legs this depends on the sub-surface hair length for slanted hairs. May help to not shave for several days so you can see which hairs are still growing. **First Update, 22 May 2011**: minor regrowth in a few areas, though I still haven't finished legs. 3~5 full-power pulses on a single hair takes a while if you're not dedicated, even if it is mostly permanent. If it's hairs in the same place that appear instead of vellus hairs converting due to hormones, it's probably because part of the follicle didn't receive enough heat. Be generous and give an extra laser pulse more than what's necessary for the hair to simply fall out, to make sure enough heat reaches all of the epithelial cells of the hair matrix. Otherwise the tiny hairs that result could be impossible to laser away, though other methods might work. If you are trying to completely remove even the smaller hairs, be sure to appropriately increase the number of pulses according to size of the hairs being treated as a smaller hair root both absorbs less heat and dissipates it more quickly between pulses. However, if you have experienced pale dots on skin from loss of melanin, you might want to just accept that small hairs might remain where larger ones were. I checked one tiny hair stub on my leg that had not fallen out, and attached to its base was a tiny new hair much smaller than the original, due to the hair production cells which did not receive enough heat when the area was treated.

So far, no noticeable difference in hair growth and/or appearance in any of the treated areas (underarms, bikini line and legs). I do not recommend this product, especially at such a high cost.

  20. I must say I was skeptical about the home laser treatments but the return policy was too good not to try it! First of all, you have to understand the why and how lasers work to remove hair. This type of laser ONLY works best on lighter skin tones with darker hair growth. And you have to be honest about the areas you want to remove....the hair on your head may be brown but the hair on your legs may be blonde. If you are looking to remove your blonde leg hair - it is not going to work. If your hair is mostly red or blonde or gray - it is probably not gonna reduce your hair growth to satisfaction. But if you can see your dark hair follicle even after you shave your legs (or wherever) - it should work just fine. If your skin is darker or too tan - check the chart on TRIA's website to make sure it will be safe for you to use...dark skin can burn! If your skin and hair tone is in the 'laser zone' - then all you gotta do is STAY ON SCHEDULE and be patient! First 3 months - you must do your areas every two weeks. After that - it is only once a month. My hairless bottom line is that it is working for me! I did my legs, bikini line, and underarms after 4 months of being on schedule and I have very little to no hair growing back. The hair that does grow back is very fine. I have been using it at the highest level - which does hurt much like a big rubber band snap. But I find if you press the laser window firmly on the skin (not just hovering the skin), it helps to dissipate the pain a little. I will keep using it, but most LPL laser literature that I have read states you will see most hair removal at 8 months. Also, it will eat up a day if you are doing several body areas at once. This is because it takes about 1.5 hours to recharge the battery after about 20 mins at the highest level. But you learn to break it up and maybe start early on a Saturday so that you can get house chores done, etc. while you are waiting for the recharge. A slight inconvenience, but what should I expect at this price!? I will post my results after 8 months!!!

  23. I'll put 5 stars because I have personally seen the Tria be effective, but this is not a review. I just felt compelled to point out something misleading: on the main page, Amazon shows three items \\"frequently bought together...\\" with the Tria. Right now, one is a pair of red-orange \\"Bynovel Laser Eye Protection Safety Glasses\\". Please know two things: 1) the Tria is designed for use without safety glasses (just don't use it anywhere near your eyes!) and 2) those specific glasses listed only protect against blue and green lasers. The Tria uses an 810 nm near-infrared laser (visually it appears a dull red color), so those glasses would not shield against it. Please don't try to use the Tria near your eyes and assume glasses or goggles designed for a different wavelength would help. Note: I do have a physics background, and I do work with Tria lasers.

  26. I have a \\"Tria\\" (Pulsed Diode Laser) and now both, a \\"Veet Infini'silk PRO\\" and a \\"Veet Infini'silk\\" made by \\"Silk'n\\" (Intense Pulsed Light = IPL) for at-home hair removal. I have also experienced both of these Hair Removal technologies (Pulsed Diode Laser/\\"PDL\\" and Intense Pulsed Light/\\"IPL\\") at Medical Spas with professional grade machines. I have fair skin and thick black hair which makes me an ideal user for all forms of Laser Hair Removal (LHR).<br /><br />It is worth mentioning that I have a condition called PCOS that causes excessive hair on women(more on this later). I have battled this since I was a teenager and I am 39 now. I started LHR in my early 20s and have experienced all forms of Laser Hair Removal (LHR) in medical settings.<br /><br />In medical spas, I have had superior results with Pulsed Diode Lasers. By this, I mean that more hair follicles died and has not regrown significantly (about 5% regrowth). With Intense Pulsed Light, the areas I had professionally treated have regrown by about 50% over the years. Having said that, I have found that the Tria and the Silk'n products are suited to different uses for me. I will explain...<br /><br />The Tria is a great product that I have extensively used. It works well, but it's main drawbacks are the tiny treatment area (about 1/4 inch round), the need to repeatedly lift the device off the skin between pulses (strains wrist/hand after a few minutes), and the need to \\"overlap\\" the pulses (impossible to do on backside areas that you can not directly see and tedious to do on large areas like legs). It is also very painful to use on coarse black hair like mine. These issues create a slow and laborious treatment experience for some areas and make it nearly impossible to treat other areas. I like to use the Tria for quick spot treatments on new hairs on easy-to-see/ easy-to-reach areas. The Tria is also my go-to device for precision work and small bony areas like face, feet, ankles, fingers, etc. Unlike the Veet Infini'Silk Pro (Silk'n), the Tria has an onboard battery so you can do your treatments on your bed or sofa or where ever you like. The disadvantage to this is that the battery is not replaceable and will eventually wear out (however, mine is still working after 6 years). The Silk'n devices have to be plugged in so you are tethered to a 6 ft cord, but there is no battery to wear out. Only the bulb cartridge wears out.<br /><br />There are some advantages to the Veet Silk'n products. The PRO version boasts a much larger treatment surface of approx. 1/2in x 1 1/4in (1.3cm x 3cm) while the smaller Infini'silk has a treatment area of .9cm x 3cm. These are MUCH larger treatment areas than the Tria (which has a treatment area about 1/3 the size of the smaller Infini'silk). Unlike the Tria, the Veet devices do not need to be lifted from the skin between pulses and the pulses do not need to be overlapped. You can just hold down the button as you \\"flash, glide, flash, glide\\" and the devices predictably and consistently flash every 3.5 seconds as you work along. The Silk'n devices have a \\"raised rectangle\\" on the heads that leaves a temporary impression on your skin that makes it very easy to see where you just treated so you neither overlap or leave gaps between pulses. With the large treatment areas and no need to overlap pulses, the Silk'n Pro allows me to treat larger and hard to see areas MUCH more quickly than the Tria. The upfront costs for the Silk'n devices are a couple hundred less than a Tria.<br /><br />I use both the Tria and the Silk'n devices on their highest settings (5). The pain from the Tria can only be described as intense. I use both ice packs and numbing cream with it. The pain from the Silk'n devices(IPL) is negligible by comparison and I have not needed any cooling or numbing for them even on sensitive areas. This was not my experience with IPL in Medical Spas. With both IPL and Laser (Ruby and Diode) Hair removal, I needed numbing before treatmentand ice packs during treatment. I do not know why the Silk'n devices are so much less painful, even on the highest setting. It may be related to the particular light wavelengths, the light filter(s) on the cartridge, the wattage, etc.<br /><br />Back to my past experience with IPL hair removal in Med spas. With only a couple of exceptions, I dreaded going to a facility to have my treatments done. For those of you that have never been for laser hair removal in a derm or med spa, it can be a harrowing experience. The powerful equipment they use is not as fool-proof as the at-home devices are. The possibility of burns is very real (I have been burned... by a doctor who was trying out his new laser without training). If you want to see what what it looks like to get burns, do a google search of \\"laser hair removal burns\\" to see what untrained technicians have done to people. Ensuring that your laser technician has been properly trained can be difficult (there is no training required in any state. Some states (not most) require that the spa simply must have a \\"doctor\\" that has agreed to put his name behind it, or that a nurse actually operate the laser... but doctors and nurses do not get laser training in med school). This is why ALL of these facilities require you to sign a broad medical and liability release that includes burns, disfiguring injuries and poor/ no results. Getting a laser technician that is trained, competent, experienced, hygienic (and makes you feel comfortable during treatment) can be very challenging. I have been told by more than one facility, that not too many people ask the questions I ask, such as \\"How do you sterilize the laser tip in between patients?\\". I walked out of more than one facility because they did not have a satisfactory answer or looked at me with puzzlement when I asked this question. With all LHR, there is a part of the device that touches the skin (genitals, butts, arm pits, faces, lips, hands, feet, wounds, rashes, skin afflictions, etc.) and can transmit disease if not sterilized between each patient. Hello! this should be a very basic protocol, but many facilities don't even bother with sanitizing the devices, much less sterilizing them between patients.<br /><br />I went through a couple of years worth of monthly treatments on several areas of my body with IPL exclusively (same technology as the Infini'silk devices). I had a wonderful, highly trained technician with multiple training certifications and significant experience with a state of the art machine. The areas I had treated with IPL lost about 70-90% of the existing hair and kept it that way for about 2 years. Slowly the hair grew back in to about 50% over the course of the next 3-4 years and then stayed that way. Alternatively, the areas that I had professionally treated with true lasers (same technology as Tria device) have remained nearly hair free for the duration of my post treatment years (7-15 years depending on when the treatments were performed). So I had \\"superior\\" results with true Laser hair removal and \\"good\\" results with IPL. If I was going back to a Med Spa for treatment, I would not do IPL again, but for home use, Yes. The advantages of the Infini'silk for large and hard to see areas are acceptable trade offs for me.<br /><br />One important point about LHR (of any kind). The only hairs that are actually killed are the ones that are zapped in the growth phase. Just because a hair falls out doesn't mean the follicle is dead. Getting hairs to fall out and actually killing them are two different things. This is the biggest reason why repeated treatments are necessary. Not all the hairs you zap are in the \\"growth phase\\". You will have to go over the same areas several times over the course of months to eventually catch all of the hairs in their growth phase. And of course, as you are zapping away, it is possible that your hormones are working against you and sprouting brand new follicles (not new hairs in the dead follicles that you have killed with the laser). IPL or laser will eventually kill all of your current hair follicles, but your body will form new ones over time. Future treatments will be needed to maintain the results. Hair growth is controlled by hormones (and genetics). In my case, because of PCOS, I will likely be doing hair removal to some degree for the rest of my life.<br /><br />There are some significant differences between the two Infini'silk devices. The biggest difference is the size of the treatment area. The Infini'silk PRO has a treatment area about 1/3 LARGER than the Infini'silk model. This may not seem like much, but if you are treating large areas of your body, this extra size makes a big difference in treatment times, i.e. The Infini'silk PRO will take you only 20 minutes to do a lower leg, while the Infini'silk will take 30 minutes to do the same area. The second big difference is that the PRO model has a replaceable bulb that lasts 5,000 pulses and the smaller Infini'silk bulb can not be replaced, but lasts 50,000 pulses. Keep in mind that the smaller unit has a smaller treatment area so it will need 3 pulses to cover the same area as 2 pulses from the PRO model. Otherwise, the units function the same way. They look different and are sized differently, but the wavelength, power and pulse duration are the same. I prefer the larger PRO model because the larger treatment area saves me time, but if you are only treating small areas like face, underarms, bikini line, etc. the Infini'silk is more than adequate.<br /><br />If you don't follow the protocols, you won't get satisfactory results. There is no cheating or shortcuts that will cause these devices to magically work. Make sure that your skin and hair colors will work with them, follow the protocol, and you will get results.<br /><br />This is a genuine review based on my first hand experience with the Tria and Veet products and my accumulated knowledge of LHR. I have a condition called PCOS that has caused excessive body hair since puberty. After some really bad bleeding, scarring and results from \\"sugaring\\", epilating, waxing and electrolysis, my parents purchased my first LHR series for me in my early 20s. I am 37 now. Over the course of my life, I have researched and tried every method of hair removal out there including every type of LHR. LHR is the only method that really made a difference and it has has changed my life for the better. I am happy to share my hard earned knowledge with others and I do this freely. I hope this review is helpful for folks looking for at-home laser hair removal.<br /><br />The other common question/objection I have received is, \\"if you have been getting laser hair removal done for years, why do you still need a Tria or Veet?\\". I think the main part of the answer to that question is already thoroughly explained in the above review and can be summed up with \\"because hormones and genetics cause brand new follicles to naturally keep forming\\", but the other part of the answer is that when I first started getting laser hair removal, the cost was $2,800 for a 8 treatments of a small area like \\"lower face\\" (which did not include cheeks or anything under the jawline). At such prices, I could only budget to do one such area per year and I had a whole body that needed treatments! As you can imagine, such a costly process takes \\"years\\". As the technology eventually became more common, prices began to come down and LHR is much more affordable now, but sadly, there is still no training or license required to operate or own one of these powerful lasers. In fact, anyone with 50k can legally buy a used pro-quality laser on the secondary market.<br /><br />Thanks for reading! I hope this review is helpful.   27. First, some background. I went through about 6 IPL sessions back in 2004/2005 and I simply ran out of money to keep paying $250 per session. For those that say that ALL hair grows back after some point with laser treatments, this is not the case for ME. I don't know for others, but after 6 sessions, and now over 5 years since my last treatment, about 60% of the hair I used to have (chest+stomach) is still gone, and I think after 5 long years one can call it \\"permanent.\\" Because so much hair was reduced over time I never saw the point in going back (I also didn't want to spend on it!) since shaving what was left was easier. So here I am 5 years later and I saw this and I said why not?! For $495 I'll finish the job finally. I have heard but cannot confirm that actual lasers are more effective than IPL, which this Tria is. So in theory this might be equal to or better than the professional treatments I got 5 years ago. If I go by the pain...they are equal (Tria at highest setting) and if that's any kind of measure of effectiveness vis-a-vis professional lasers then I think I can be optimistic! UPDATE: I did about 5 sessions total on my chest and stomach and the verdict is this: it did not work for me. I honestly did not see results at all. I wish I could say I did, especially given the serious, serious flaws this product has. Even if it had worked, I would still NOT recommend this product. Why? It has some major ergonomic and usability flaws that make it an absolute pain to use. At times you would rather stay hairy than go through the motions with this product. Where to begin? 1. It is very heavy--if you plan on doing hard to reach areas, the weight will get to your arm very quickly. 2. The covered area is 1cm squared--literally tiny. It would take me 30 minutes to get through 1/2 of my chest, and remember I already had permanent reduction from previous salon treatments. If you have more hairs, those 30 minutes would be 45. 3. Because of it's tiny area, you needso many more zaps--depleting the battery very very quickly. You are left with having to wait 3 hours while it charges until you can continue your treatment. 2 whole legs I would imagine would take a day and half to complete. 4. The enormous head, combined with the tiny laser area makes it almost impossible to see where you have zapped. I experience redness longer than most- I have this condition that makes me dermographic and drives my allergist crazy- my skin reacts to everything and stays redder longer. I have a quick fix for it ladies (also works when you wax your brows!)- keep some Visine Advanced Relief in the fridge and apply to clean, dry skin. Closes up those capillaries, so you can get out of the house faster without your face saying \\"I just rug-burned my chin!!!! Wanna Guess Howwwww???!!!\\" Hair follicles- occasionally, I'll get a bump, pimple-type. It's not RIGHT after using Tria it's a few days after when hairs want to grow in. I need lots of exfoliation and found that if I apply a lotion with alpha-hydroxy acid in it (I used the Alpha-Hydrox brand foot cream, it's got 12% AHA and it works everywhere, not just on your feet, at a much lower cost than the \\"soufflé\\"). Also, sometimes those \\"zapped\\" hairs look kind of weird (how I can tell Tria got them- they look thicker, flatter) and on occasion they've either popped out like a pimple or I've gently pulled them out with a tweezer to help things along, because who needs MORE dark pores looking like grody blackheads? Also, it says to use on a fresh shave. I disagree. Shave the night before and use in the morning or vice versa so the Tria can \\"see\\" the follicles better. Sometimes a too-close shave takes away too much of my dark hair (which oddly comes out really dark at the ends but is lighter at the follicle itself) and I find it's more effective with at least 12 hours growth but not much more. Do yourself a favor and use Tria in winter and spring when you're at your pastiest, ashen, mousiest self (speaking solely on my own account of course). You'll see the fastest, most effective results. Once you start getting that sun on you it won't work as well and it \\"knows\\" when there's not enough contrast to work with the little test gun that comes with it you MUST use to turn it on every time (don't cheat. you're just cheating yourself). I was in shock the first time I got a \\"red\\" no-go light, but also pleased that I'd gotten over winter. Point is, plan accordingly and use winter to transform you like Fuzzy Wuzzy. As an aside, I've never had professional laser. My similarly fair skinned/dark haired friend did, and it burned the he** out of her and left considerably scarring as one other poster mentioned. She signed so many disclaimers thatsuing was not really an option (she worked in a law firm!). That scared the bejesus out of me, so I gave up ever considering it unless I had the time to invest in finding someone with 100% patient satisfaction (um.... it's been 20 years now). The TRIA doesn't operate on the same extremes. I doubt it's as painful as professional, and even at the top setting IMO it's about like having an elastic snapped on a tiny spot on your skin. It's no big deal. If it bothers you, don't spent a lot of money on pricey lidocaine treatments, get some after-sun aloe lotion. It contains the same lidocaine and the aloe is good for you. When this one dies on me, I'll buy another. Further, based on my experience with the company and device, I'd considering buying their blue-light treatment for skin.

  74. I just purchased the product yesterday and completed the first treatment and I will update the review over the course of treatments to accurately reflect its quality. However, my initial impressions of the product are good. I am the ideal candidate for laser hair removal, light skin with dark hair, and have had tremendous success with professional treatments. But as most people interested in the product, I was attracted by the overall cost benefit when compared to purchasing a series of treatments. The physical product itself seems well-crafted and sturdy. Easy to hold, aim, and pulse and no little parts that you have to worry about keeping track of. I would say to anyone interested in purchasing the product that you must be completely realistic about what you're looking to achieve and what this sort of technology is capable of. If you have thick coarse hair all over your body like a gorilla this device will NOT leave you as smooth as a baby's bum. The energy density of the laser isn't strong enough to do the sort of damage required for extensive hair follicle reduction and your results even with a medical grade laser won't leave you entirely smooth. I purchased the unit more as a supplement to the professional treatments that I am getting and to reduce(not completely remove/retard) hair growth in different areas. I'd say it's most appropriate for dealing with armpits, forearms, bikini, feet/toes, and while they say it's not suitable for the face or neck I am a man and purchased it for precisely that reason to deal with the stray hairs that the professional laser may have missed. The laser head is pretty narrow and unless you're a very diligent and patient person, purchasing this to do your legs might not bed the best option. They also recommend that you begin on the lowest setting so that you gradually adjust to the pain, but even at the highest setting, the power of the laser is far below what the standard medspa laser is shooting, so suck it up anddeal with the pain of setting 5 if you're looking to achieve real results. Settings 1-3 will garner you NOTHING. I recommend turning it to level 5 and testing it on the top of your foot to get some practice in before you start treating your problem areas. One major difference between this laser and what you will get done in a spa is the lack of a cooling device. Most medspa lasers simultaneously shoot out a spurt of cold air to minimize the pain and heat caused by the laser. This is not a feature of Tria therefore I recommend filling a ziptop bag with ice and as you pulse the area you place the bag of ice immediately over the area. Hope that helps people who are contemplating purchasing the item. I'll let you know in the long-term what my thoughts are.

  95. I am a male in my early 20's. I purchased the Tria three months ago in the hope that it would eliminate or reduce my body hair on everywhere except my head legs and eyebrows. I have done as much research as possible online and have been frustrated by the lack of detailed and fully credible reviews, so I am going to summarize my experience and research here. 1. Effectiveness: The Tria is not going to permanently eliminate all hair in any area. It simply is not powerful enough for that. This is borne out by the specifications if you look on any credible hair removal website as well as reviews from people who used it and then eventually *stopped* using it. However, it is extremely effective on dark, coarse hair on light skin. For dark, coarse, thick hair it will generally destroy the follicle or damage it significantly enough that the hair that grows back will be vellus hair (light, fuzzy, and somewhat slower growing). However, although it may not look like it is the case, there are vellus hairs already there even in a thick, coarse, hairy area. The Tria will not eliminate these vellus hairs and will not eliminate lighter and thinner hairs. It will however often cause them to shed temporarily. This is why it is considered permanent hair reduction, and not permanent removal. Hairs that have been treated will stop growing noticeably almost immediately and will shed on their own within two weeks. 2. Pain: On thick, coarse hair I used the highest setting, which was quite painful. I often used a combination of Advil, Vicodin, and an ice pack to make it tolerable. Then again I have a low pain tolerance, and you can use a lower setting. I just prefer to bear the pain to maximize the effectiveness. 3. Technique: To be most effective, I found that zapping an area as many as 3-5 times in one sitting was the best thing to do. I liked to pluck the hairs with a tweezer after lasering them. Although you will not find that recommended elsewhere, I found it to be a very effective way to test the efficacy of the laser. If the hairs slid right out with no resistance at all, they would come out with the bulb just as they do in electrolysis, and that suggests the follicle is completely destroyed. If there is any resistance, stop pulling and laser some more. If you cannot pull the hair with no resistance, give up, and don't pluck it - it will probably fall out but does not seem to be permanent, although it will damage the hair and make it finer. You will need to continue periodic treatments for a year or more to catch hairs that cycle from dormant to the growth phase. 4. Overall Value: As long as your expectations are reasonable, the Tria provides excellent value for the money. Professional laser treatments are very expensive and time consuming and if you really want to eliminate all hair I would suggest using the Tria for a long time period and then getting a professional laser treatment or two. That way you save some money and get rid of a chunk of the hair at minimal cost. 5. Some More Suggestions: The treatment head is small and the battery lasts a decently long time but you will need multiple treatments to cover a full area. Make sure you overlap as the instructions say for maximum effectiveness. If you are targeting particular hairs keep in mind you need to hit the root which may not be directly below the hair but slightly to its side under the skin, so laser around it as well. If you come across very stubborn hairs then I would suggest a home electrolysis or second hand professional electrolysis machine to take them out. Electrolysis is far too slow and expensive for me for all my hair especially since I am a guy and it is not critical to remove it, but it is great for touch up. Do not use this on moles. Also it will be more painful if your skin is darker or if you use it on darker areas of your body. It targets melanin, which is what causes skin and hair color. If anyone has any other questions please post comments. Also check the comment section as I will post follow ups to this review.

Your existing hair follicles will disappear but it is absolutely possible that new ones can grow in! That's the trick - the existing ones are permanent but new ones can grow in! (ah ha - the truth! I got it out of technician finally!!)<br /><br />Now, with that being said, I still LOVE laser hair removal and I do LOVE my Tria! Here is why:<br /><br />I started going to laser hair removal salons about seven years ago. I have pale skin (but I love to tan in the summer), freckles and dark, coarse hair. I have tried them all - literally, all of them (purely laser, gel treatments, on skin, away from skin)! Some great, some not so great and at various salons which will remain nameless.<br /><br />After 1 year of treatment, I definitely saw major hair reduction, but as some other users said it started coming back eventually...new hair follicles! Tried the next salon, felt the same thing...the treatment wasn't working. New hair follicles will CONSTANTLY grow in! However, looking back to how much I've had to shave and the razor burn I've gotten over the years, I have to say that I do love the Tria because it actually does work as maintenance.<br /><br />That is the thing with this product! You have to keep using it! New hair follicles always, always comes back - whether you use this product or a different one or go to a salon. But, the difference, after a couple of years, is really dramatic. I used to shave my legs and have spikey hair hours later. Now, I can go a week without shaving and you can barely notice. I'm Spanish - I have a lot of hair - everywhere! My bikini - forget it - been bare for years! Hairs start growing in? Zap with the Tria and I'm good for 6 months!<br /><br />The reason I give the Tria 4 stars and not 5 is because like other users - the small head is really annoying. Where as other systems charge you the same base price but then you constantly have to replace the laser heards - not the Tria.<br /><br />The only area where I truly used the Tria (and no previous salons) were my underarms. I did not follow the schedule because as other users stated - this laser hurts! I actually found it more painful than some salon lasers. However, my hair has definitely gotten softer. It's not fully gone because I couldn't take the pain, but if you stick with it, this laser does what it's supposed to do. And again, after time to time maintenance, it will get better! I promise!<br /><br />Trust me, I'm hairy, I've done my homework over the years...the only process that truly permanently removes hair is Electrolysis and that is PAINFUL and really expensive!<br /><br />Now, if you're a former waxer and are now converting to the Tria - be warned that this may not work well for you! Waxing, over time, damages the hair follicles! (Waxing salons won't tell you that) so the Tria has a harder job to do and therefore, you will not get the best results either. However, as I started - keep using the Tria. I know it's painful ladies, but this is the price of beauty unfortunately.<br /><br />Just don't expect these mind blowing hair eliminating results...everyone person is different, and everyone has a different rate of hair follicles growing back.<br /><br />Having this at home to do maintenance as opposed to going back to the salon (scheduling appointments, waiting, driving there, back, doing the treatments - you waste the same amount of time) - having it is awesome! I really do love it. But you will still have to shave! However, as my dark hair ladies will see - having light blond hairs grow in that you can't see is SO worth over time! I haven't hadrazor burn in years!<br /><br />Good luck everyone!

  225. I purchased this device after hearing recommendations from my sisters, but I was a little disappointed in the efficacy of the machine. To shed some light on whether or not you should try it, here's an explanation as to how these devices work and whether or not it will work for you:<br /><br />To preface, I have had about 12 sessions of professional laser hair removal on several parts of my body over the last 6 years (5 sessions every 6 weeks followed by touch ups - no hormone problems, I just have more hair than most women). Understand how the laser works, and you will know if it works for you.<br /><br />A laser hair removal device, whether the Tria or a giant machine used in clinics, finds pigment (color) and passes energy all the way through the pigment to the root of the hair. It then kills the root, thereby disabling that hair forever. Unfortunately, we have several hairs that pass through the same follicle, so that's why you often need to have several treatments, because you cannot kill the entire hair follicle with just one session. Hair doesn't all grow at once, either, which is why you have to space out treatments (the laser cannot kill hair that hasn't grown yet). As long as that hair follicle is still in tact, hair will continue to grow from it.<br /><br />If you have light skin and dark hair, the machine can \\"find\\" the pigment more easily and send energy all the way to the root. If you have light hair (or light roots), then the laser will not send enough energy through the hair to kill it at the root, and hence it will not work. If you have too dark of skin, the laser will not be able to differentiate hair from skin, and will not work. If you have freckles and moles, you may notice the laser \\"stings\\" over those area as it is sending energy into a non-hair area.<br /><br />The laser only works in one way: either it kills the hair at the root or it doesn't. There is no middle ground. How do you know if the laser killed the hair at the root? Afteryou treat it with the laser, you will be able to pull the hair out of your skin with a tweezer (or even your fingers) and it will easily slip out of the skin as it will no longer be attached at the root. If you go to pull it out and it's still attached at the root (you may even see the root when you pull it out - or it will be resistant to pulling and hurt on its way out), then the laser did not kill that root and hair will continue to grow from that follicle. The laser either kills the hair at the root or it doesn't. It is just that simple.<br /><br />So how do you know if this device works? Well, doing several passes on my underarms, going over the same spot twice each time, I'd say about 30% of the hair each session gets killed at the root. The rest of the hair the laser either misses, doesn't pass enough energy through, or the hair is too light. The reality is this is a tiny, battery powered device. The machines used by professionals are massive and can heat up a room 20 degrees F. This device is nowhere's near powerful enough to get the job done without multiple sessions.<br /><br />When people complain that they use this over and over again and they don't see any results, what they really need to be asking is \\"did this kill the root of the hair?\\" It's possible the laser IS working, slowly but surely, but you just have so much hair that it requires several treatment sessions. This device will not kill the root of the hair like professional machines will.<br /><br />Overall I would not recommend this product to people who have never had laser professionally. It is OK for those who have done several laser treatments with a professional and are looking for a \\"touch up\\" device. But I think this would only work on light skin and dark hair, as the laser on the highest setting (5) kills only about 30% of my hair when following the directions perfectly. If you're looking to do large areas like your legs, save your money and find a Groupon or Living Social deal for a local laser hair removal place. I will say that the device isn't painful. I was able to do 4 on my bikini and 5 on my underarms without more than a slight discomfort.

Within this time, I am able to get about half of one ankle done (I'm small too). According to the directions- you take the laser head, apply it to you skin and wait for it to pulse. Each pulse takes about 5 seconds to fire (doesn't sound like a big deal, but those 5 seconds add up). The you move the treatment head to the next spot, about 3 cm to make the next pulse and so on. You have to overlap the pulses (the directions show you a 'map' for your pulses, which is circles representing the treatment head, overlapping half way on top of each other (just like a Venn Diagram). if you could hold the laser in your hand and see how small the treatment head is, you'd understand how long the correct process takes.<br />It's just not efficient for large areas. The ease of adjusting the power is very easy, making pain and discomfort unnecessary.With the adjustable power settings, in more sensitive areas I dropped down one power level and felt no pain or discomfort. The power settings start at 1 for the lowest and 5 at the highest. For my legs, I was able to comfortably use the level 4 power setting and around the bikini area a level 3 without discomfort. I believe that it is important for users to know that the higher power settings will bring about faster results. So, you have to balance pain with the time investment you are willing to make.<br /><br />Operation: 5 stars out of 5.<br />The controls are very easy and straightforward. After just a five minute tutorial, you can start using this product immediately without complication or confusion.<br /><br />Product Design: 3 stars out of 5.<br />The laser head is small and it would be nicer if it was about twice the size. At times, the shape can be difficult to get into hard to reach or more curved areas like under arms. The laser head can only operate on a mostly flat surface. So, underarms, shin bones, and knees can take some negotiation to get a flat enough surface for the laser to fire.<br /><br />Weight: 3 stars out of 5.<br />The weight isn't bad and seems to weigh the same as a full sized hand held hair dryer, but the weight is packed into the size of a travel hair dryer. It is a bit top heavy and the handle is comfortable, but long.<br /><br />Battery life: 3 stars out of 5.<br />The approximate battery life is around 45 minutes. When I first started, I could get both legs done before the battery would need to be recharged. Once recharged, I could then finish up my bikini line and under arms. Now that I have so much less area to treat, I can spot treat as needed on a single battery charge.<br /><br />Battery Recharge Time: 3 stars out of 5.<br />Depending on which setting you select for the charging session, it can take anywhere from two hours or up to six hours to recharge.<br /><br />Noise Level: 3 stars out of 5.<br />As the laser fires, the audible beep is not bothersome at all. However, when the fan turns on, it is about the same level of noise as a hair dryer on the low setting. I originally thought I'd do my treatments while watching a movie, but when the fan turns on, I have to turn up the sound on the t.v. which can be distracting.<br /><br />Product Instruction and Construction Quality: 5 stars out of 5.<br />Tria has very good instructional videos and manuals with the product. The product itself seems well constructed and durable. The product packaging is nicely designed and visually attractive.<br /><br />Convenience: 5 stars out of 5.<br />You just can't beat being able to do your own laser hair treatment in the privacy of your own home at your own convenience.<br /><br />Value: 5 stars out of 5.<br />Though it seems a little pricey at time of purchase, when I compare the $450 I wasted at a medical salon, the Tria is an excellent investment. I'm guessing that I will be hair free after three more treatments. That means that I was able to do my legs from the knees down, bikini line, and underarms all for under $400. I can do touch ups at no additional cost. I never have to make appointments and I can do this in the comfort of my own home.<br /><br />Overall Rating: 4 stars out of 5.<br />Though there are some minor improvements that could be made, the results are very pleasing. It is important for potential buyers to be honest with themselves about their hair and skin coloring. And, it is equally important to be realistic about the time frame for realizing the true results of the product. I believe for buyers who abide by the previous two suggestions, you will be very satisfied with this product just like I have been.
